The Prophetic Testimony for Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Ibn Asakir cites two narrations linking a Quranic verse to al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two narrations interpret Quran 5:54 as referring to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his lineage.

Core Idea
The Quranic verse 'Soon Allah will bring a people' points to al-Ash'ari through his grandfather.

Imam Ibn Asakir presents two independent traditions that connect the Quranic verse 5:54 directly to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. These narrations serve to counter accusations against the Ash'ari school by grounding its founder in scriptural and prophetic authority. The passage shows how later scholars used hadith to legitimize theological figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice that it contains two distinct narrations separated by a repetition of the phrase 'قال الامام الحافظ رضی عنه'.
The first narration is from a scroll, the second from a book.
2
Identify the two narrations
In your own words, summarize what each narration says about the verse and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Pay attention to the chain of transmission for each.
3
Understand the link to Abu Musa
Why does the Prophet point to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari? How does that connect to Abu al-Hasan?
Abu Musa is the grandfather of Abu al-Hasan.
4
Reflect on the purpose
What is the author trying to prove by including these narrations? Consider the sectarian context.
This legitimizes al-Ash'ari as a divinely favored imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الامام الحافظ رضی عنه نقلت هذه الخطوط على نصها من ذلك الدرج ونقلها غيرى من الفقهاء وتفسير قول هذا الفارسي : هذا أبو الحسن كان إماما ولما أنزل عز وجل قوله ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) أشار المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى رضى الله عنه وقال هم قوم هذا. قال الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه : قرأت فى كتاب أبي يعقوب يوسف ابن علی بن محمد المؤدب الذي قرأه على أبى الفتوح بن عباس عن عبيد بل تفسيره : أبو الحسن الأشعرى هذا امام انزل الله عزل وجل في شأنه هذه الآية ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) وأشار النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم لما نزلت إلى جده أبي موسى الأشعرى وقال ( هم قوم هذا ).
Imam al-Hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I copied these lines exactly as they were from that scroll, and others among the jurists copied them. The interpretation of the Persian's statement: This Abu al-Hasan was an imam. When Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed His words 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him,' the Chosen One, peace be upon him, pointed to Abu Musa, may Allah be pleased with him, and said, 'They are this people's people.' Imam al-Hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: I read in the book of Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Mu'addib, which he read to Abu al-Futuh ibn Abbas from Ubayd, the interpretation: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is this imam. Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed this verse concerning him: 'Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him,' and the Prophet, peace be upon him, when it was revealed, pointed to his grandfather Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said, 'They are this people's people.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents two independent chains of narration that interpret the Quranic verse 5:54 as referring to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (d. 324/935), the founder of the Ash'ari school of theology. The first narration comes from Imam al-Hafiz (likely Ibn 'Asakir himself), who transmits from a scroll written by 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Isfarayini and others, including a Persian gloss identifying 'this Abu al-Hasan' as an imam, and stating that when the verse was revealed, the Prophet Muhammad pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (the grandfather of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari) and said 'They are this people's people' — meaning the descendants of Abu Musa. The second narration is from the book of Abu Ya'qub al-Mu'addib, who transmits via two intermediaries that the verse was revealed concerning Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari himself, and that the Prophet pointed to his grandfather Abu Musa. Both narrations serve to legitimize al-Ash'ari as a divinely favored figure, using scriptural and prophetic testimony to counter his detractors.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
فسوف يأتي الله بقوم
أبو موسى الأشعري
إمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Quran 5:54 refers to the companions in general and not specifically to the lineage of al-Ash'ari.
Correction: The narrations explicitly state that the verse was revealed concerning Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, with the Prophet pointing to his grandfather Abu Musa as the progenitor of the people mentioned.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, to whom did the Prophet point when the verse 'فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه' was revealed?
A) Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
B) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
C) The Persians
D) The Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Two independent narrations link Quran 5:54 to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, using prophetic testimony to legitimize his status as an imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet himself pointed to the grandfather of al-Ash'ari, what does that mean for your attitude toward the Ash'ari school? Are you prepared to accept its teachings as part of the prophetic tradition, even if you previously dismissed them?
?
Sectarian bias often leads us to reject even authentic narrations. After reading these two reports, can you honestly say you would have accepted them if they came from a tradition you normally oppose? How will you change your approach to evaluating such testimonies?

Al-Juwayni's Defense of al-Ash'ari from False Accusations
Al-Juwayni defends al-Ash'ari from false accusations on ijtihad and other issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false accusations made against al-Ash'ari and how al-Juwayni refuted them based on al-Ash'ari's own writings.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's own books prove the slanders against him false.

In this passage, the great Ash'ari theologian Imam al-Juwayni writes a spirited defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari against a series of accusations made by innovators. After clarifying al-Ash'ari's position on ijtihad—where he held that all mujtahids are correct in subsidiary matters—al-Juwayni lists several false attributions and declares that he has examined al-Ash'ari's works and found them to be the opposite of what his detractors claim. This lesson will help you see how early Ash'ari scholars defended their founder's legacy from distortion.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Juwayni's opening on ijtihad
Notice how al-Juwayni distinguishes between principles (usul) and branches (furu') regarding who is correct among the mujtahids. This sets the stage for al-Ash'ari's view.
Al-Ash'ari held that all mujtahids are correct in branches, which differed from al-Shafi'i's own position.
2
Identify the list of false accusations
Al-Juwayni enumerates several claims made by the innovators against al-Ash'ari: denying the Qur'an in the mushaf, denying a prophet in his grave, exception in faith, negation of pre-eternal power, takfir of commoners, and obligating knowledge of proofs.
These are serious theological charges that could undermine al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy.
3
Understand al-Juwayni's refutation
Al-Juwayni states that he examined al-Ash'ari's books and found all these accusations to be false. He attributes the slanders to envy because al-Ash'ari exposed the errors of the innovators.
This shows the importance of returning to primary sources rather than relying on hearsay.
4
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider why it matters that al-Ash'ari's true positions are defended. This passage demonstrates the early Ash'ari commitment to textual verification and protects the founder from misrepresentation.
The same principle applies today: we must verify claims about scholars from their own works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الشيخ الامام ركن الدين أبو محمد عبد الله بن يوسف الجويني رحمه الله في آخر كتاب صنفه وسماه عقيدة أصحاب الامام المطلبي الشافعي رضي الله عنه وكافة أهل السنة والجماعة وقال : ونعتقد ان المصيب من اجتهدين في الأصول والفروع واحد ويجب التعيين في الأصول فأما في الفروع فربما يتأتى التعيين وربما لايتأتى ومذهب الشيخ أبي الحسن رحمه تصويب المجتهدين في الفروع وليس ذلك مذهب الشافعي رضي الله عنه وأبو الحسن احد أصحاب الشافعى رضى الله عنهم، فإذا خالفه في شيء ا عرضنا عنه فيه ومن هذا القبيل قوله ان لاصيغة للأمر وتقل وتعز مخالفته أصول الشافعى رضى الله عنه، ونصوصه وربما نسب المبتدعون إليه أنه يقول ليس فى المصحف قرآن ولا في القبر نبي، وكذلك الاستثناء في الإيمان ونفى قدرة الخلق فى الأزل وتكفير العوام وايجاب علم الدليل عليهم وقد تصفحت ما تصفحت من كتبه وتأملت نصوصه في هذه المسائل فوجدتها كلها خلاف ما نسب إليه ولا عجب ان اعترضوا عليه واخترصوا فإنه رحمه فاضح القدرية وعامة المبتدعة وكاشف عوراتهم ولا خير فيمن لا يعرف حاسده.
And the Shaykh Imam Rukn al-Din Abu Muhammad Abdullah ibn Yusuf al-Juwayni, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned at the end of a book he authored, which he named 'The Creed of the Followers of Imam al-Muttalibi al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, and all the People of the Sunnah and the Community,' and said: We believe that the one who is correct among those who exert independent judgment (mujtahidun) in principles (usul) and branches (furu') is one, and specification (ta'yin) is obligatory in principles. As for branches, specification may be attained and may not be attained. The school of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, is to declare all mujtahids correct in the branches, and that is not the school of al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him. Abu al-Hasan is one of the followers of al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with them. So if he contradicts him in something, we turn away from him in that. Among this is his statement that there is no verbal form (sigha) for the command, a view that is rare and mighty, and his contradiction of the principles and texts of al-Shafi'i. The innovators sometimes attribute to him that he says there is no Quran in the mushaf and no prophet in the grave, likewise exceptive statements (istithna') in faith, negation of the creatures' power in pre-eternity, declaring the common people disbelievers (takfir al-'awamm), and making knowledge of the proof obligatory upon them. And I have examined what I have examined of his books and contemplated his texts on these issues, and I found them all contrary to what is attributed to him. And it is no wonder that they opposed him and summarized, for he, may Allah have mercy on him, exposed the Qadariyya and all innovators and uncovered their weaknesses, and there is no good in one who does not know his envier.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a theological and historical defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari by Imam al-Juwayni (d. 478/1085), a leading Ash'ari theologian. Al-Juwayni writes in his book on creed, stating the Ash'ari position on ijtihad: in fundamental principles (usul al-din), only one mujtahid is correct and specification of the correct view is necessary, while in subsidiary legal rulings (furu'), multiple correct views are possible. He notes that al-Ash'ari held the view that all mujtahids are correct in branches, which differs from al-Shafi'i's own position. Al-Juwayni then addresses accusations made by innovators against al-Ash'ari: that he denied that the Quran is in the mushaf (i.e., the physical book), that he denied that a prophet is in his grave (i.e., bodily life), that he made exception in faith (i.e., saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'), that he negated the creatures' capacity for action in pre-eternity, that he declared the common people disbelievers, and that he required knowledge of theological proofs for salvation. Al-Juwayni asserts that after examining al-Ash'ari's own writings, he found these accusations to be false. He attributes these accusations to the innovators' hatred, because al-Ash'ari exposed their errors and weaknesses.

Key Terms
المجتهدين
الأصول والفروع
التصويب
المبتدعون
الاستثناء في الإيمان
تكفير العوام
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari denied that the Quran is in the physical mushaf and that the Prophet is alive in his grave.
Correction: Al-Juwayni states that after examining al-Ash'ari's own writings, he found these claims to be false. Al-Ash'ari's actual positions are contrary to these accusations.

Checkpoint
According to al-Juwayni, what did al-Ash'ari hold regarding the ijtihad of scholars in subsidiary legal rulings?
A) Only one mujtahid is correct
B) All mujtahids are correct
C) No ijtihad is permissible
D) Only the first four generations are correct

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's true theological positions can be verified from his own writings, which refute the slanders of his opponents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What false claims have you accepted about a scholar or group without verifying from their own writings? How can you—starting today—commit to reading primary sources before forming judgments?
?
Al-Juwayni defended al-Ash'ari by examining his books. Is there a scholar you have misunderstood or criticized based on hearsay? Will you seek out their actual works to correct your understanding?
?
The innovators slandered al-Ash'ari out of envy because he exposed their errors. Whose errors are you afraid to confront because it might provoke hostility? How will you embody the courage of al-Juwayni in defending the truth?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Mihna and the Early Sunni Mutakallimun
Ibn Asakir describes the Mihna and the early Sunni mutakallimun's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the context of the Mihna and how early Sunni mutakallimun defended orthodoxy against the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The Mihna was a crucible that forged Sunni theology through patient refutation.

The early Abbasid era saw a state-imposed inquisition enforcing the Mu'tazilite doctrine of a created Quran. Sunni scholars faced immense pressure, yet a group of pious theologians quietly authored defenses of the faith. This passage from Ibn Asakir sets the stage for the emergence of a towering defender: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mihna history
Read about the trial under al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, and how Ahmad ibn Hanbal's refusal to debate was used against the Sunnis.
The term 'Mihna' refers to the inquisition, a period of persecution.
2
Identify the early Sunni theologians
Notice the names of early mutakallimun who refuted the Mu'tazila without mixing with them: Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, Abdullah ibn Kullab.
These scholars combined asceticism with theological refutation.
3
Reflect on their strategy
Consider why they avoided direct contact with innovators yet wrote books against them. What does this say about their approach?
This sets the stage for al-Ash'ari's different approach later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نا أبو عبد الله محمد بن موسی بن عمار الكلاعى المايرقى الفقيه قال : أعظم ما كانت المحنة یعنی زمن المأمون والمعتصم، فتورع من مجادلتهم أحمد بن حنبل رضی الله عنه فمو هوا بذلك على الملوك وقالوا لهم انهم يعنون أهل السنة يفرون من المناظرة، لما يعلمونه من ضعفهم عن نصرة الباطل، وأنهم لا حجة بأيديهم وشتعوا بذلك عليهم حتى امتحن في زمانهم أحمد بن حنبل وغيره فأخذ الناس حينئذ بالقول بخلق القرآن، حتى ما كان تقبل شهادة شاهد ولا يستقضى قاض ولا يفتي مفت لا يقول بخلق القرآن، وكان في ذلك الوقت من المتكلمين جماعة كعبد العزيز المكي والحارث المحاسبي وعبدالله ابن كلاب وجماعة غيرهم، وكانوا أولى زهد وتقشف لم ير أحد منهم أن يطأ لأهل البدع بساطا ولا ان يداخلهم فكانوا يردون عليهم ويؤلفون الكتب في إدحاض حججهم، إلى ان نشأ بعدهم وعاصر بعضهم بالبصرة أيام اسماعيل القاضي ببغداد أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل بن أبي بشر الأشعرى رضى الله عنه وصنف فى هذا العلم لأهل السنة التصانيف وألف لهم التواليف حتى أدحض حجج المعتزلة وكسر شوكتهم، وكان يقصدهم بنفسه يناظرهم فكلم فى ذلك وقيل له كيف تخالط أهل البدع وتقصدهم بنفسك، وقد أمرت بهجرهم فقال هم فقال هم أولو رياسة منهم الوالي والقاضي ولرياستهم لا ينزلون إلى فإذا كانوا هم لا ينزلون الى ولا أسير انا إليهم فكيف يظهر الحق ويعلمون ان لأهل السنة ناصرا بالحجة، وكان أكثر مناظرته مع الجبائي المعتزلى وله معه في الظهور عليه مجالس كثيرة فلما كثرت تواليفه ونصر مذهب السنة وبسطه تعلق بها أهل السنة من المالكية والشافعية وبعض الحنفية، فأهل السنة بالمغرب والمشرق بلسانه يتكلمون وبحجته يحتجون، وله من التواليف والتصانيف ما لا يحصى كثرة، وكان ألف في القرآن كتابه الملقب بالمختزن ذكر لى بعض أصحابنا أنه رأى منه طرفا وكان بلغ سورة الكهف وقد انتهى مائة كتاب، ولم يترك آية تعلق بها بدعى إلا أبطل تعلقه بها، وجعلها حجة لأهل الحق وبين المجمل وشرح المشكل، ومن وقف على تواليفه رأى ان الله تعالى قد أمده بمواد توفيقه وأقامه لنصرة الحق والذب عن طريقه، وكان فى مذهبه مالكيا على مذهب أهل الحجاز.
Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ammar al-Kala'i al-Mayiraqi al-Faqih narrated: The greatest trial was during the time of al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim. Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with him, refrained from debating them, so they used that to deceive the rulers and said about them (the People of Sunnah) that they flee from debate because they know their own weakness in supporting falsehood and that they have no proof. They slandered them with that until Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others were put to trial. At that time, the people adopted the saying that the Quran is created, so much so that no witness's testimony was accepted, no judge was appointed, and no mufti gave fatwa unless he said the Quran is created. At that time, there was a group of mutakallimun (speculative theologians) such as Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, Abdullah ibn Kullab, and others. They were people of asceticism and piety; none of them would set foot on the carpet of the people of innovation or mix with them. They would refute them and author books to demolish their arguments. Then, after them, and contemporary with some of them in Basra during the days of Isma'il al-Qadi in Baghdad, arose Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Abi Bishr al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him. He authored for the People of Sunnah books on this science, and wrote compilations for them until he demolished the arguments of the Mu'tazila and broke their power. He used to go to them in person to debate. He was spoken to about that and asked: 'How can you mix with the people of innovation and go to them in person, when you have been commanded to avoid them?' He replied: 'They are people of authority; among them are the governor and the judge, and because of their authority they do not come down to me. So if they do not come down to me, and I do not go to them, how can the truth become manifest and they know that the People of Sunnah have a helper by argument?' Most of his debates were with al-Jubba'i the Mu'tazili, and he had many sessions with him in which he triumphed over him. When his writings became numerous and he supported and spread the Sunni school, the People of Sunnah among the Malikis, Shafi'is, and some Hanafis adhered to it. Thus the People of Sunnah in the West and the East speak with his tongue and argue with his proof. His compilations and writings are too numerous to count. He authored a book on the Quran entitled al-Mukhtazan; some of our companions told me they saw a portion of it, and it had reached Surah al-Kahf, and it amounted to one hundred books. He did not leave a single verse that an innovator clung to except he invalidated their clinging to it, and made it a proof for the people of truth, clarified the ambiguous, and explained the problematic. Whoever examines his writings will see that Allah Almighty supplied him with the materials of His success and raised him to support the truth and defend His path. He was, in his school, a Maliki, on the school of the people of the Hijaz.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative describing the early 'Mihna' (inquisition) under the Abbasid caliphs al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, when the Mu'tazila doctrine of the created Quran was enforced. Ahmad ibn Hanbal famously refused to debate the Mu'tazila, and his stance was used to accuse the Sunni community of fleeing from debate. The pressure was so great that public positions required accepting the createdness of the Quran. During this time, a group of early Sunni mutakallimun—such as Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, and Abdullah ibn Kullab—engaged in refuting the Mu'tazila while maintaining asceticism and avoiding direct mixing. Then, after them, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari emerged in Basra, contemporaneous with some of them. He authored works for the Sunnis, refuted the Mu'tazila, and debated them personally. When criticized for associating with innovators, he explained that he had to go to them because they were rulers and would not come to him; only by engaging could the truth prevail. His main opponent was al-Jubba'i, the leading Mu'tazili. Al-Ash'ari's writings became so influential that Sunnis across the Malikis, Shafi'is, and some Hanafis adopted his approach. His work on the Quran, al-Mukhtazan, was a massive commentary refuting innovative interpretations. The passage concludes with praise that Allah granted him success and that he was a Maliki in fiqh.

Key Terms
المحنة
خلق القرآن
المتكلمون
عبد العزيز المكي
الحارث المحاسبي
عبد الله بن كلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the early Sunni mutakallimun were silent or passive during the Mihna.
Correction: They actively wrote books to demolish the Mu'tazila arguments, though they avoided direct debate.

Checkpoint
Who was the Sunni scholar that refrained from debating the Mu'tazila, leading to accusations of weakness?
A) Abd al-Aziz al-Makki
B) Ahmad ibn Hanbal
C) Al-Harith al-Muhasibi
D) Abdullah ibn Kullab

Key Takeaway
The Mihna forced Sunnis to articulate their beliefs under pressure, and early mutakallimun laid the groundwork for later defenses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face social or institutional pressure to conform to a belief you know is false, do you have the courage of Imam Ahmad to refuse—even when it means being slandered as weak? What would it take for you to stand firm like him?
?
The early mutakallimun combined deep piety with intellectual defense of the faith. Is your own spiritual discipline fueling your ability to defend the truth, or are they disconnected? What is one concrete step you can take to bridge them this week?
?
The Mu'tazila accused the Sunnis of fleeing debate out of weakness. Have you ever avoided defending your faith because you feared you wouldn't have the right answers? What can you learn from the mutakallimun's approach of quiet preparation and written refutation?

Al-Ash'ari's Emergence and Debating Strategy
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ash'ari's emergence and his approach to debating the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari emerged as a defender of Sunnah and why he personally engaged Mu'tazila in debate.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari went to the Mu'tazila because they would not come to him.

After the early mutakallimun, a new figure arose: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. He took a different approach, actively going to the Mu'tazila to debate them. When criticized for mixing with innovators, he gave a compelling justification rooted in the pursuit of truth. This segment captures his distinct methodology and his famous debates with al-Jubba'i.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ash'ari's rise
Notice the timeline: after the earlier scholars, al-Ash'ari appeared in Basra and began authoring works for the Sunnis.
He is described as demolishing Mu'tazila arguments.
2
Understand his debating strategy
He would go to them in person. The passage records a question about why he mixes with innovators and his answer.
Focus on his justification: the Mu'tazila held authority and would not descend.
3
Analyze his main debates
His opponents included al-Jubba'i, the leading Mu'tazili. He triumphed in many sessions.
This shows his effectiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نا أبو عبد الله محمد بن موسی بن عمار الكلاعى المايرقى الفقيه قال : أعظم ما كانت المحنة یعنی زمن المأمون والمعتصم، فتورع من مجادلتهم أحمد بن حنبل رضی الله عنه فمو هوا بذلك على الملوك وقالوا لهم انهم يعنون أهل السنة يفرون من المناظرة، لما يعلمونه من ضعفهم عن نصرة الباطل، وأنهم لا حجة بأيديهم وشتعوا بذلك عليهم حتى امتحن في زمانهم أحمد بن حنبل وغيره فأخذ الناس حينئذ بالقول بخلق القرآن، حتى ما كان تقبل شهادة شاهد ولا يستقضى قاض ولا يفتي مفت لا يقول بخلق القرآن، وكان في ذلك الوقت من المتكلمين جماعة كعبد العزيز المكي والحارث المحاسبي وعبدالله ابن كلاب وجماعة غيرهم، وكانوا أولى زهد وتقشف لم ير أحد منهم أن يطأ لأهل البدع بساطا ولا ان يداخلهم فكانوا يردون عليهم ويؤلفون الكتب في إدحاض حججهم، إلى ان نشأ بعدهم وعاصر بعضهم بالبصرة أيام اسماعيل القاضي ببغداد أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل بن أبي بشر الأشعرى رضى الله عنه وصنف فى هذا العلم لأهل السنة التصانيف وألف لهم التواليف حتى أدحض حجج المعتزلة وكسر شوكتهم، وكان يقصدهم بنفسه يناظرهم فكلم فى ذلك وقيل له كيف تخالط أهل البدع وتقصدهم بنفسك، وقد أمرت بهجرهم فقال هم فقال هم أولو رياسة منهم الوالي والقاضي ولرياستهم لا ينزلون إلى فإذا كانوا هم لا ينزلون الى ولا أسير انا إليهم فكيف يظهر الحق ويعلمون ان لأهل السنة ناصرا بالحجة، وكان أكثر مناظرته مع الجبائي المعتزلى وله معه في الظهور عليه مجالس كثيرة فلما كثرت تواليفه ونصر مذهب السنة وبسطه تعلق بها أهل السنة من المالكية والشافعية وبعض الحنفية، فأهل السنة بالمغرب والمشرق بلسانه يتكلمون وبحجته يحتجون، وله من التواليف والتصانيف ما لا يحصى كثرة، وكان ألف في القرآن كتابه الملقب بالمختزن ذكر لى بعض أصحابنا أنه رأى منه طرفا وكان بلغ سورة الكهف وقد انتهى مائة كتاب، ولم يترك آية تعلق بها بدعى إلا أبطل تعلقه بها، وجعلها حجة لأهل الحق وبين المجمل وشرح المشكل، ومن وقف على تواليفه رأى ان الله تعالى قد أمده بمواد توفيقه وأقامه لنصرة الحق والذب عن طريقه، وكان فى مذهبه مالكيا على مذهب أهل الحجاز.
Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ammar al-Kala'i al-Mayiraqi al-Faqih narrated: The greatest trial was during the time of al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim. Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with him, refrained from debating them, so they used that to deceive the rulers and said about them (the People of Sunnah) that they flee from debate because they know their own weakness in supporting falsehood and that they have no proof. They slandered them with that until Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others were put to trial. At that time, the people adopted the saying that the Quran is created, so much so that no witness's testimony was accepted, no judge was appointed, and no mufti gave fatwa unless he said the Quran is created. At that time, there was a group of mutakallimun (speculative theologians) such as Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, Abdullah ibn Kullab, and others. They were people of asceticism and piety; none of them would set foot on the carpet of the people of innovation or mix with them. They would refute them and author books to demolish their arguments. Then, after them, and contemporary with some of them in Basra during the days of Isma'il al-Qadi in Baghdad, arose Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Abi Bishr al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him. He authored for the People of Sunnah books on this science, and wrote compilations for them until he demolished the arguments of the Mu'tazila and broke their power. He used to go to them in person to debate. He was spoken to about that and asked: 'How can you mix with the people of innovation and go to them in person, when you have been commanded to avoid them?' He replied: 'They are people of authority; among them are the governor and the judge, and because of their authority they do not come down to me. So if they do not come down to me, and I do not go to them, how can the truth become manifest and they know that the People of Sunnah have a helper by argument?' Most of his debates were with al-Jubba'i the Mu'tazili, and he had many sessions with him in which he triumphed over him. When his writings became numerous and he supported and spread the Sunni school, the People of Sunnah among the Malikis, Shafi'is, and some Hanafis adhered to it. Thus the People of Sunnah in the West and the East speak with his tongue and argue with his proof. His compilations and writings are too numerous to count. He authored a book on the Quran entitled al-Mukhtazan; some of our companions told me they saw a portion of it, and it had reached Surah al-Kahf, and it amounted to one hundred books. He did not leave a single verse that an innovator clung to except he invalidated their clinging to it, and made it a proof for the people of truth, clarified the ambiguous, and explained the problematic. Whoever examines his writings will see that Allah Almighty supplied him with the materials of His success and raised him to support the truth and defend His path. He was, in his school, a Maliki, on the school of the people of the Hijaz.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative describing the early 'Mihna' (inquisition) under the Abbasid caliphs al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, when the Mu'tazila doctrine of the created Quran was enforced. Ahmad ibn Hanbal famously refused to debate the Mu'tazila, and his stance was used to accuse the Sunni community of fleeing from debate. The pressure was so great that public positions required accepting the createdness of the Quran. During this time, a group of early Sunni mutakallimun—such as Abd al-Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, and Abdullah ibn Kullab—engaged in refuting the Mu'tazila while maintaining asceticism and avoiding direct mixing. Then, after them, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari emerged in Basra, contemporaneous with some of them. He authored works for the Sunnis, refuted the Mu'tazila, and debated them personally. When criticized for associating with innovators, he explained that he had to go to them because they were rulers and would not come to him; only by engaging could the truth prevail. His main opponent was al-Jubba'i, the leading Mu'tazili. Al-Ash'ari's writings became so influential that Sunnis across the Malikis, Shafi'is, and some Hanafis adopted his approach. His work on the Quran, al-Mukhtazan, was a massive commentary refuting innovative interpretations. The passage concludes with praise that Allah granted him success and that he was a Maliki in fiqh.

Key Terms
الأشعري
الجبائي
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari compromised his principles by mixing with innovators.
Correction: He had a valid strategic reason: to reveal the truth to those in authority who would not come to him.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Ash'ari go to the Mu'tazila to debate?
A) He was forced by the caliph
B) They would not come to him due to their authority
C) He wanted to learn from them
D) He had no choice

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's willingness to engage opponents directly, despite criticism, was key to spreading Sunni doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone in error who holds a position of authority in your community, do you avoid them out of fear of confrontation or seek to engage them with the truth? What do your actions reveal about your priorities?
?
Al-Ash'ari risked criticism from fellow Sunnis to make the truth known. What comfort or reputation are you clinging to that prevents you from speaking truth to power or reaching out to those in error?
?
If you were in al-Ash'ari's place, would you have the courage to go against the common practice of avoidance and engage those in authority? What would need to change in your heart to become that bold?

Al-Ash'ari's Legacy and Writings
Ibn Asakir describes the impact of al-Ash'ari's writings and his famous book al-Mukhtazan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the vast impact of al-Ash'ari's writings on Sunni scholarship and his methodology in defending the Quran against innovations.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's systematic refutations became the standard for Sunni theology.

The final part of Ibn Asakir's account celebrates the lasting influence of al-Ash'ari. His prolific writings, especially the massive commentary al-Mukhtazan, systematically refuted every innovational interpretation of the Quran. Sunnis across the globe adopted his arguments. This passage also mentions his Maliki affiliation, grounding him in traditional fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Appreciate the scale of his influence
Note that Sunnis in the East and West adopted his arguments, and his works became foundational.
This shows the widespread acceptance of his method.
2
Learn about al-Mukhtazan
This book on the Quran was so extensive that it reached Surah al-Kahf in one hundred volumes. It refuted every innovator's misuse of verses.
It demonstrates his thoroughness.
3
Recognize his fiqh background
He was a Maliki, following the school of the people of Hijaz, grounding his theology in traditional jurisprudence.
This counters claims that he abandoned fiqh for kalam.

?

?
Al-Ash'ari's writings united Sunni scholars from different madhhabs. But today, where do you see disunity? Are you part of the problem or the solution? Will you actively seek to learn from scholars of other madhhabs and defend the common Sunni creed, even when it costs you your comfort?
?

Or do you take their legacy for granted? Commit now to read one work of a Sunni theologian this month with that gaze of gratitude and awe.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Mihna and the Early Sunni Response
Ibn Asakir narrates the context of the Mihna and early Sunni refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of the Mihna and how early Sunni scholars defended orthodox theology through scholarly refutation without direct engagement with innovators.

Core Idea
The trial forced Sunnis to articulate their creed through written refutation.

Ibn Asakir begins by describing the greatest trial (Mihna) under al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, when the Mu'tazila used state power to force the doctrine of the created Qur'an. He then highlights a group of early Sunni mutakallimun who, though ascetic and avoiding direct contact with innovators, wrote books to invalidate their arguments. This lesson sets the stage for the later emergence of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Mihna
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the political and theological pressure described. The Mu'tazila defamed Ahmad ibn Hanbal and forced the creationist doctrine on society.
The passage mentions that even court witnesses and judges were required to affirm creationism.
2
Reflect on Ahmad ibn Hanbal's stance
Ahmad ibn Hanbal refrained from debating the Mu'tazila. The text says he 'abstained from debating them' (فتورع من مجادلتهم). Consider why he might have done so.
This was used by the Mu'tazila to claim that Sunnis had no arguments.
3
Identify the early Sunni mutakallimun
Look for the names mentioned: 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, 'Abdallah ibn Kullab, and others. Note their approach: they did not sit with innovators but wrote books to refute them.
This shows that Sunni theological defense existed before al-Ash'ari.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعظم ما كانت المحنة یعنی زمن المأمون والمعتصم، فتورع من مجادلتهم أحمد بن حنبل رضی الله عنه فمو هوا بذلك على الملوك وقالوا لهم انهم يعنون أهل السنة يفرون من المناظرة، لما يعلمونه من ضعفهم عن نصرة الباطل، وأنهم لا حجة بأيديهم وشتعوا بذلك عليهم حتى امتحن في زمانهم أحمد بن حنبل وغيره فأخذ الناس حينئذ بالقول بخلق القرآن، حتى ما كان تقبل شهادة شاهد ولا يستقضى قاض ولا يفتي مفت لا يقول بخلق القرآن، وكان في ذلك الوقت من المتكلمين جماعة كعبد العزيز المكي والحارث المحاسبي وعبدالله ابن كلاب وجماعة غيرهم، وكانوا أولى زهد وتقشف لم ير أحد منهم أن يطأ لأهل البدع بساطا ولا ان يداخلهم فكانوا يردون عليهم ويؤلفون الكتب في إدحاض حججهم، إلى ان نشأ بعدهم وعاصر بعضهم بالبصرة أيام اسماعيل القاضي ببغداد أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل بن أبي بشر الأشعرى رضى الله عنه وصنف فى هذا العلم لأهل السنة التصانيف وألف لهم التواليف حتى أدحض حجج المعتزلة وكسر شوكتهم، وكان يقصدهم بنفسه يناظرهم فكلم فى ذلك وقيل له كيف تخالط أهل البدع وتقصدهم بنفسك، وقد أمرت بهجرهم فقال هم فقال هم أولو رياسة منهم الوالي والقاضي ولرياستهم لا ينزلون إلى فإذا كانوا هم لا ينزلون الى ولا أسير انا إليهم فكيف يظهر الحق ويعلمون ان لأهل السنة ناصرا بالحجة، وكان أكثر مناظرته مع الجبائي المعتزلى وله معه في الظهور عليه مجالس كثيرة فلما كثرت ،تواليفه ونصر مذهب السنة وبسطه تعلق بها أهل السنة من المالكية والشافعية وبعض الحنفية، فأهل السنة بالمغرب والمشرق بلسانه يتكلمون وبحجته يحتجون، وله من التواليف والتصانيف ما لا يحصى كثرة، وكان ألف في القرآن كتابه الملقب بالمختزن ذكر لى بعض أصحابنا أنه رأى منه طرفا وكان بلغ سورة الكهف وقد انتهى مائة كتاب، ولم يترك آية تعلق بها بدعى إلا أبطل تعلقه بها، وجعلها حجة لأهل الحق وبين المجمل وشرح المشكل، ومن وقف على تواليفه رأى ان الله تعالى قد أمـذه نمواد توفيقه وأقامه لنصرة الحق والذب عن طريقه، وكان فى مذهبـه مـالـكـيـا علـى مذهب مالك بن أنس رضى الله عنه، وقد كان ذكر لى بعض من لقيت من الشافعية انه كان شافعيا حتى لقيت الشيخ الفاضل رافعا الحمال الفقيه فذكر لي عن شيوخه ان ابا الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه كان مالكيا فنسب من تعلق اليوم بمذهب أهل السنة وتفقه فى معرفة أصول الدين من سائر المذاهب إلى الأشعرى لكثرة تواليفه وكثرة قراءة الناس لها ولم يكن هو أول متكلم بلسان أهل السنة إنما جرى على سنن غيره وعلى نصرة مذهب معروف فزاد المذهب حجة وبيانا ولم يبتدع مقالة اخترعها ولا مذهبا انفرد به ألا ترى أن مذهب أهل المدينة ينسب إلى مالك بن أنس الله عنه كان على مذهب أهل المدينة يقال له مالكي ومالك ومن الله رضی عنه إنما جرى على سنن من كان قبله وكان كثير الاتباع لهم إلا أنه زاد المذهب بيانا وبسطا وحجة وشرحا والف كتابه الموطأ وما أخد عنه الأسمعة والفتاوى فنسب المذهب إليه لكثرة بسطه له وكلامه فيه من فكذلك أبو الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه لا فرق
The greatest trial was during the time of al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim. Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah be pleased with him) refrained from debating them, so they [the authorities] used that to defame him before the kings, and they said to them: 'They (meaning the Ahl al-Sunnah) flee from debate because they know their weakness in supporting falsehood, and they have no proof in their hands.' They defamed them with that until Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others were tested in their time. Then the people adopted the saying that the Qur'an is created, so much so that no witness's testimony was accepted, no judge was appointed, and no mufti gave a fatwa unless he said the Qur'an is created. At that time there was a group of mutakallimun like 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, 'Abdallah ibn Kullab, and others. They were foremost in asceticism and scrupulousness; none of them was seen to step on a rug for the people of innovation nor to mix with them. They would refute them and write books to invalidate their arguments, until there arose after them and contemporaneous with some of them in Basra during the days of Isma'il al-Qadi in Baghdad: Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Abi Bishr al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him). He authored works in this science for the Ahl al-Sunnah and composed writings for them until he invalidated the arguments of the Mu'tazila and broke their power. He would go to them himself and debate them. He was criticized for that and asked: 'How can you mix with the people of innovation and go to them yourself, when you have been commanded to shun them?' He replied: 'They are people in positions of leadership, including the governor and the judge, and due to their status they do not come down to me. If they do not come down to me and I do not go to them, how will the truth become apparent and they know that the Ahl al-Sunnah have a supporter by argument?' Most of his debates were with al-Jubba'i al-Mu'tazili, and he had many sessions with him in which he prevailed over him. When his writings multiplied, he supported the Sunnah and spread it, and the Ahl al-Sunnah among the Malikiyya, Shafi'iyya, and some Hanafiyya adhered to it. Thus the Ahl al-Sunnah in the Maghrib and the Mashriq speak with his tongue and argue with his proof. He has writings and works beyond count. He authored a book on the Qur'an called al-Mukhtazin; one of our companions told me he saw a portion of it and it had reached Surat al-Kahf, and it comprised one hundred books. Every verse that an innovator clung to, he invalidated that clinging and made it a proof for the people of truth. He clarified the ambiguous and explained the problematic. Whoever examines his works sees that Allah Almighty aided him with the materials of His success and established him for the support of truth and defense of His path. He was, in his madhhab, a Maliki upon the madhhab of Malik ibn Anas (may Allah be pleased with him). Some of the Shafi'iyya I met told me he was a Shafi'i, until I met the virtuous Shaykh Rafi' al-Hammal al-Faqih, who told me based on his teachers that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) was a Maliki. Thus whoever today clings to the madhhab of the Ahl al-Sunnah and studies the principles of religion from among the various schools is attributed to al-Ash'ari due to the abundance of his writings and people's frequent reading of them. He was not the first mutakallim to speak in the tongue of the Ahl al-Sunnah; rather, he followed the path of others and supported a known madhhab, increasing it with proof and clarification. He did not innovate a new statement nor a madhhab unique to himself. Do you not see that the madhhab of the people of Madina is attributed to Malik ibn Anas? He was upon the madhhab of the people of Madina, but he is called a Maliki. Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) merely followed the way of those before him, and he had many followers, except that he increased the madhhab in clarification, expansion, proof, and explanation, and authored his book al-Muwatta', from which reports and fatwas were taken. Thus the madhhab was attributed to him due to his extensive elaboration and speech in it. Similarly, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) – no difference.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a historical and biographical account by Ibn Asakir. It first describes the context of the Mihna under al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, where the Mu'tazila pressured the authorities and Ahmad ibn Hanbal refrained from debating, leading to propaganda against the Ahl al-Sunnah as being unable to defend themselves. The forced adoption of the doctrine of the createdness of the Qur'an is described, and the early Sunni mutakallimun: 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, 'Abdallah ibn Kullab and others, who refuted the innovators through writings. Then the rise of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is narrated: he compiled works for the Sunnis, debated the Mu'tazila in person despite criticism, explaining that he went to them because they held high positions and would not come to him. His main opponent was al-Jubba'i. His writings became authoritative for Sunnis of all schools – Malikis, Shafi'is, and Hanafis. The author mentions a massive Quranic work (al-Mukhtazin) that reached one hundred volumes. Al-Ash'ari is described as refuting every innovator's proof by turning it into a Sunni proof. The passage then addresses the issue of al-Ash'ari's madhhab: according to some sources he was a Maliki, though some Shafi'is claimed him. Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari did not invent a new madhhab but only clarified and expanded the existing Sunni school, analogously to Malik ibn Anas, who likewise followed predecessors and was not an innovator. The comparison is explicit: one does not say Malik invented a new school; similarly, al-Ash'ari is not an innovator.

Key Terms
المحنة
خلق القرآن
أحمد بن حنبل
عبد العزيز المكي
الحارث المحاسبي
عبدالله بن كلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That early Sunni scholars avoided theological argument entirely and only later did al-Ash'ari engage in kalam.
Correction: The passage shows that scholars like Ibn Kullab wrote refutations and engaged in theological discourse, but they did so through books, not personal debate with innovators.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Ahmad ibn Hanbal refrain from debating the Mu'tazila?
A) Because he was weak in argument and feared losing.
B) Because he abstained out of scrupulousness (turawu').
C) Because he was ordered by the ruler not to debate.
D) Because he agreed with them on the createdness of the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Before al-Ash'ari, Sunni scholars defended orthodoxy through written refutations while maintaining distance from innovators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you conformed to a false belief or practice due to social or institutional pressure? What specific step will you take this week to cultivate the courage to stand for the truth, even at personal cost?
?
The early Sunni scholars wrote refutations from a distance, avoiding direct association with innovators. Are you more concerned with protecting your reputation or actively defending the truth? Identify one area where you have remained silent and commit to speaking out in the next week.
?
If your livelihood or social standing depended on affirming something against your conviction, would you pass the test as Ahmad ibn Hanbal did? What weakness in your own character needs immediate strengthening to prepare for such a trial?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
9 min
Al-Ash'ari's Defense of Sunni Theology
Ibn Asakir narrates the life, debates, writings, and madhhab of al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari defended and systematized Sunni theology through direct debate and extensive writing, and why he is not considered an innovator of a new sect.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari defended the Sunni creed by engaging opponents directly and authoring comprehensive refutations.

Continuing from the earlier context, Ibn Asakir now introduces Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as the one who boldly engaged the Mu'tazila face-to-face to demonstrate the strength of the Sunni position. This lesson explores his justification for such engagement, his monumental writings, and the issue of his madhhab. Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari did not invent a new madhhab but merely clarified and expanded the existing Sunni school, analogous to Malik ibn Anas.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ash'ari's emergence and debates
Read the passage starting from 'وعاصر بعضهم' to understand how al-Ash'ari personally went to debate the Mu'tazila, especially al-Jubba'i.
Notice his response to critics: he went because they held high positions and would not come to him.
2
Analyze his justification for debating
Al-Ash'ari argued that if he did not go to them, the truth would never reach them. This shows his proactive approach to da'wa.
3
Examine his writings
Note the mention of his book al-Mukhtazin, which was an extensive commentary on the Qur'an refuting every innovator's misinterpretation.
The author says it reached one hundred books by Surat al-Kahf.
4
Understand the analogy with Malik
Ibn Asakir compares al-Ash'ari to Malik ibn Anas: both followed predecessors and expanded the madhhab, not innovating.
This corrects the misconception that al-Ash'ari founded a new sect.

أعظم ما كانت المحنة یعنی زمن المأمون والمعتصم، فتورع من مجادلتهم أحمد بن حنبل رضی الله عنه فمو هوا بذلك على الملوك وقالوا لهم انهم يعنون أهل السنة يفرون من المناظرة، لما يعلمونه من ضعفهم عن نصرة الباطل، وأنهم لا حجة بأيديهم وشتعوا بذلك عليهم حتى امتحن في زمانهم أحمد بن حنبل وغيره فأخذ الناس حينئذ بالقول بخلق القرآن، حتى ما كان تقبل شهادة شاهد ولا يستقضى قاض ولا يفتي مفت لا يقول بخلق القرآن، وكان في ذلك الوقت من المتكلمين جماعة كعبد العزيز المكي والحارث المحاسبي وعبدالله ابن كلاب وجماعة غيرهم، وكانوا أولى زهد وتقشف لم ير أحد منهم أن يطأ لأهل البدع بساطا ولا ان يداخلهم فكانوا يردون عليهم ينزلون إلى فإذا كانوا هم لا ينزلون الى ولا أسير انا إليهم فكيف يظهر الحق ويعلمون ان لأهل السنة ناصرا بالحجة، وكان أكثر مناظرته مع الجبائي المعتزلى وله معه في الظهور عليه مجالس كثيرة فلما كثرت ،تواليفه ونصر مذهب السنة وبسطه تعلق بها أهل السنة من المالكية والشافعية وبعض الحنفية، فأهل السنة بالمغرب والمشرق بلسانه يتكلمون وبحجته يحتجون، وله من التواليف والتصانيف ما لا يحصى كثرة، وكان ألف في القرآن كتابه الملقب بالمختزن ذكر لى بعض أصحابنا أنه رأى منه طرفا وكان بلغ سورة الكهف وقد انتهى مائة كتاب، ولم يترك آية تعلق بها بدعى إلا أبطل تعلقه بها، وجعلها حجة لأهل الحق وبين المجمل وشرح المشكل، ومن وقف على تواليفه رأى ان الله تعالى قد أمـذه نمواد توفيقه وأقامه لنصرة الحق والذب عن طريقه، وكان فى مذهبـه مـالـكـيـا علـى مذهب مالك بن أنس رضى الله عنه، وقد كان ذكر لى بعض من لقيت من الشافعية انه كان شافعيا حتى لقيت الشيخ الفاضل رافعا الحمال الفقيه فذكر لي عن شيوخه ان ابا الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه كان مالكيا فنسب من تعلق اليوم بمذهب أهل السنة وتفقه فى معرفة أصول الدين من سائر المذاهب إلى الأشعرى لكثرة تواليفه وكثرة قراءة الناس لها ولم يكن هو أول متكلم بلسان أهل السنة إنما جرى على سنن غيره وعلى نصرة مذهب معروف فزاد المذهب حجة وبيانا ولم يبتدع مقالة اخترعها ولا مذهبا انفرد به ألا ترى أن مذهب أهل المدينة ينسب إلى مالك بن أنس الله عنه كان على مذهب أهل المدينة يقال له مالكي ومالك ومن الله رضی عنه إنما جرى على سنن من كان قبله وكان كثير الاتباع لهم إلا أنه زاد المذهب بيانا وبسطا وحجة وشرحا والف كتابه الموطأ وما أخد عنه الأسمعة والفتاوى فنسب المذهب إليه لكثرة بسطه له وكلامه فيه من فكذلك أبو الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه لا فرق
The greatest trial was during the time of al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim. Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah be pleased with him) refrained from debating them, so they [the authorities] used that to defame him before the kings, and they said to them: 'They (meaning the Ahl al-Sunnah) flee from debate because they know their weakness in supporting falsehood, and they have no proof in their hands.' They defamed them with that until Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others were tested in their time. Then the people adopted the saying that the Qur'an is created, so much so that no witness's testimony was accepted, no judge was appointed, and no mufti gave a fatwa unless he said the Qur'an is created. At that time there was a group of mutakallimun like 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, 'Abdallah ibn Kullab, and others. They were foremost in asceticism and scrupulousness; none of them was seen to step on a rug for the people of innovation nor to mix with them. They would refute them and write books to invalidate their arguments, until there arose after them and contemporaneous with some of them in Basra during the days of Isma'il al-Qadi in Baghdad: Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Abi Bishr al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him). He authored works in this science for the Ahl al-Sunnah and composed writings for them until he invalidated the arguments of the Mu'tazila and broke their power. He would go to them himself and debate them. He was criticized for that and asked: 'How can you mix with the people of innovation and go to them yourself, when you have been commanded to shun them?' He replied: 'They are people in positions of leadership, including the governor and the judge, and due to their status they do not come down to me. If they do not come down to me and I do not go to them, how will the truth become apparent and they know that the Ahl al-Sunnah have a supporter by argument?' Most of his debates were with al-Jubba'i al-Mu'tazili, and he had many sessions with him in which he prevailed over him. When his writings multiplied, he supported the Sunnah and spread it, and the Ahl al-Sunnah among the Malikiyya, Shafi'iyya, and some Hanafiyya adhered to it. Thus the Ahl al-Sunnah in the Maghrib and the Mashriq speak with his tongue and argue with his proof. He has writings and works beyond count. He authored a book on the Qur'an called al-Mukhtazin; one of our companions told me he saw a portion of it and it had reached Surat al-Kahf, and it comprised one hundred books. Every verse that an innovator clung to, he invalidated that clinging and made it a proof for the people of truth. He clarified the ambiguous and explained the problematic. Whoever examines his works sees that Allah Almighty aided him with the materials of His success and established him for the support of truth and defense of His path. He was, in his madhhab, a Maliki upon the madhhab of Malik ibn Anas (may Allah be pleased with him). Some of the Shafi'iyya I met told me he was a Shafi'i, until I met the virtuous Shaykh Rafi' al-Hammal al-Faqih, who told me based on his teachers that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) was a Maliki. Thus whoever today clings to the madhhab of the Ahl al-Sunnah and studies the principles of religion from among the various schools is attributed to al-Ash'ari due to the abundance of his writings and people's frequent reading of them. He was not the first mutakallim to speak in the tongue of the Ahl al-Sunnah; rather, he followed the path of others and supported a known madhhab, increasing it with proof and clarification. He did not innovate a new statement nor a madhhab unique to himself. Do you not see that the madhhab of the people of Madina is attributed to Malik ibn Anas? He was upon the madhhab of the people of Madina, but he is called a Maliki. Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) merely followed the way of those before him, and he had many followers, except that he increased the madhhab in clarification, expansion, proof, and explanation, and authored his book al-Muwatta', from which reports and fatwas were taken. Thus the madhhab was attributed to him due to his extensive elaboration and speech in it. Similarly, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may Allah be pleased with him) – no difference.

Commentary
This passage is a historical and biographical account by Ibn Asakir. It first describes the context of the Mihna under al-Ma'mun and al-Mu'tasim, where the Mu'tazila pressured the authorities and Ahmad ibn Hanbal refrained from debating, leading to propaganda against the Ahl al-Sunnah as being unable to defend themselves. The forced adoption of the doctrine of the createdness of the Qur'an is described, and the early Sunni mutakallimun: 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Makki, al-Harith al-Muhasibi, 'Abdallah ibn Kullab and others, who refuted the innovators through writings. Then the rise of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is narrated: he compiled works for the Sunnis, debated the Mu'tazila in person despite criticism, explaining that he went to them because they held high positions and would not come to him. His main opponent was al-Jubba'i. His writings became authoritative for Sunnis of all schools – Malikis, Shafi'is, and Hanafis. The author mentions a massive Quranic work (al-Mukhtazin) that reached one hundred volumes. Al-Ash'ari is described as refuting every innovator's proof by turning it into a Sunni proof. The passage then addresses the issue of al-Ash'ari's madhhab: according to some sources he was a Maliki, though some Shafi'is claimed him. Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari did not invent a new madhhab but only clarified and expanded the existing Sunni school, analogously to Malik ibn Anas, who likewise followed predecessors and was not an innovator. The comparison is explicit: one does not say Malik invented a new school; similarly, al-Ash'ari is not an innovator.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari founded a completely new theological sect (Ash'arism).
Correction: Ibn Asakir explicitly states that he only followed the path of earlier Sunni scholars and expanded on the existing madhhab, similar to how Malik ibn Anas did not create a new madhhab but clarified the way of the people of Madina.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Ash'ari go to debate the Mu'tazila in person, according to Ibn Asakir?
A) Because he was ordered by the caliph.
B) Because they were in positions of leadership and would not come to him, so he went to them for the truth to become apparent.
C) Because he wanted to gain fame through debating.
D) Because he was forced to do so.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari defended and systematized the Sunni creed through direct engagement and extensive writing, but he did not invent a new madhhab; he expanded the existing tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari personally went to debate opponents despite criticism. When you face someone who disagrees with your religious beliefs, do you actively engage them or withdraw? What is the one fear that prevents you from going to them with the truth — and will you ask Allah to remove it this week?
?
He wrote hundred of books to refute every misinterpretation. What one area of your faith (e.g., attributes of Allah, predestination) have you not studied enough to defend? Commit today to spend 15 minutes this week learning the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah for that point.
?
Many attribute themselves to al-Ash'ari as a label, but the lesson shows he only followed the path of those before him. Ask yourself: do you follow your madhhab or group because of conviction in its truth, or because of family, culture, or comfort? Will you examine your intention before Allah tonight?

Political Support for Sunnism and the Mu'tazili Dismissal
Ibn Asakir describes the spread of Ash'ari's students and the role of King Fanakhisraw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of political patronage in the spread of Ash'ari teachings and the Mu'tazili perception of Sunnis.

Core Idea
Political support can amplify a theological school's influence.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's history shows that the Ash'ari school did not spread by scholarship alone. It highlights the role of King Fanakhisraw, a Persian ruler who loved learning, and the dismissive attitude of a Mu'tazili chief qadi toward Sunnis. Understanding this context helps explain the later Sunni resurgence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the key figures: Ash'ari's students, King Fanakhisraw, and the Mu'tazili qadi.
2
Identify the political context
Notice that the Mu'tazila were powerful in Iraq until the king's time. The king himself was a patron of scholars and hosted debates.
This shows that theological schools often needed political backing.
3
Analyze the qadi's response
Read the qadi's dismissal of Sunnis as 'a rabble of taqlid'. What does this reveal about Mu'tazili attitudes?
It reflects a common critique that Sunnis relied on tradition without rational discernment.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how this passage shows that political patronage was a factor in the spread of Ash'ari teachings, even when Sunnis were intellectually dismissed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنجب من تلامذته خلق كثير بالمشرق وكانت شوكة المعتزلة بالعراق شديدة إلى ان كان زمن الملك فناخسره، وكان ملكا يحب العلم والعلماء وكانت له مجالس يقعد فيها للعلماء ومناظرتهم، وكان قاضي القضاة في وقته معتزليا فقال له فناخسره يوما هذا المجلس عامر من العلماء إلا أنى لا أرى أحدا من أهل السنة والأثبات ينصر مذهبه فقال له : ان هؤلاء القوم عامة رعاع اصحاب تقليد وأخبار وروايات يروون الخبر وضده ويعتقدونهما وأحدهما ناسخ للثاني
There emerged from his students a great many in the East. The power of the Mu'tazila in Iraq was strong until the time of King Fanakhisraw. He was a king who loved knowledge and scholars, and he held assemblies where scholars would sit and debate. The chief qadi in his time was a Mu'tazili. Fanakhisraw said to him one day: 'This assembly is full of scholars, but I do not see anyone from the Ahl al-Sunnah and the upholders [of tradition] defending their madhhab.' He replied: 'These people are generally a rabble of followers of taqlid, reports, and narrations; they narrate a report and its opposite, believing both, while one of them is abrogating the other.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage continues the historical account of the Ash'ari school. It states that many distinguished students emerged from al-Ash'ari's teaching in the East (the Mashriq). The Mu'tazila still held strong power in Iraq until the reign of King Fanakhisraw (a Persian king, likely a Buyid ruler). This king loved learning and held assemblies for scholarly debates. The chief qadi at that time was a Mu'tazili. One day the king remarked that the assembly was full of scholars but he did not see any Sunni or traditionist (ahl al-sunnah wa al-athbat) defending their madhhab. The qadi replied dismissively, characterizing the Sunnis as mere followers of tradition (taqlid) who narrate contradictory reports and accept both without the ability to distinguish, implying they are intellectually weak. This sets the stage for later Sunni resurgence.

قاضي القضاة
شوكة المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Ash'ari school spread only through scholarship, ignoring the role of political patronage.
Correction: This passage shows that political support from King Fanakhisraw created an opening for Sunni voices, even though the Mu'tazili qadi dismissed them. Patronage was a key factor.

Checkpoint

A) He admitted the strength of Sunni arguments.
B) He dismissed Sunnis as a rabble of taqlid who cannot distinguish between contradictory reports.

D) He converted to the Sunni school.

Key Takeaway
The spread of Ash'ari teachings was aided by political patronage, even when Sunnis were intellectually dismissed by Mu'tazili elites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazili qadi dismissed the Sunnis as a 'rabble' of blind followers. Have you ever been in a situation where your beliefs were belittled by someone in authority? When that happens, do you retreat or seek to defend your faith with knowledge and confidence? What is the one step you will take this week to prepare yourself to give a reasoned defense of your creed?
?
King Fanakhisraw was open to hearing arguments from both sides, even when the powerful qadi dismissed one. In your own circles—family, work, community—do you give a fair hearing to truths that challenge the dominant narrative? Or do you silently let dismissive comments pass? Ask Allah to make you a seeker of truth like that king, and commit to speaking up next time you hear the truth being marginalized.
?
The qadi accused Sunnis of holding contradictory reports without discernment. Read the hadith and Quran with a critical heart: do you accept everything you hear about your religion without checking its authenticity or meaning? When did you last verify the source and context of a religious teaching you follow? Set a specific intention to study one foundational text deeply this week, not for others, but for your own certainty before Allah.

The Judge's Dedication and the Heretics' Joy at His Death
Describes the judge's devotion to teaching and the heretics' joy at his death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the judge's devotion to teaching and the significance of the heretics' joy at his death as an indicator of his role in defending orthodoxy.

Core Idea
A fortress against innovation: the judge's life and death reveal the battle between truth and falsehood.

This lesson presents a biographical vignette of a judge (al-qadi) who was a staunch defender of Sunni Islam. The passage highlights his tireless teaching and the reaction of heretics to his death. Through this narrative, we gain insight into the historical context of the struggle against innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the author begins by qualifying the judge's actions with intention, then moves to describe his teaching routine, his role as a fortress, the heretics' joy, and finally his students.
The passage is a single continuous sentence in Arabic.
2
Identify the two key aspects
Identify the description of the judge's dedication (teaching day and night) and the heretics' reaction (joy at his death). Consider why these two details are placed together.
3
Reflect on the legacy
The passage ends by mentioning his students who spread across lands. Reflect on how this legacy contrasts with the heretics' joy and reinforces the judge's importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا لحسن سريرته ونيته واحتسابه ذلك عند ربه وذكر من فضله كثيرا، وحكى بعض شيوخنا أن القاضى كان يدرس نهاره وأكثر ليله وكان حصنا من حصون المسلمين، وما سر أهل البدعة بشيء كسرورهم بموته رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه إلا أنه خلف بعده من تلاميذه جماعة كثيرة تفرقوا في البلاد أكثرهم بالعراق وخراسان ونزل منهم إلى المغرب رجلان
Except for the goodness of his innermost self and his intention and his reckoning of that with his Lord, and he mentioned much of his virtue. And some of our teachers narrated that the judge used to teach during his day and most of his night, and he was a fortress from the fortresses of the Muslims. And the people of innovation never rejoiced in anything like their joy at his death, may Allah have mercy on him and His pleasure. Except that he left behind him from his students a large group who scattered in the lands, most of them in Iraq and Khorasan, and from them there descended into the Maghreb two men.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note about a judge (al-qadi), praising his devotion to teaching and his role as a fortress for Muslims. The passage then transitions to mention that he left many students, most in Iraq and Khorasan, and two came to the Maghreb.

أهل البدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: The text explicitly states that they never rejoiced in anything like their joy at his death, indicating they were pleased because he was a strong opponent.

?

Abu Abdullah al-Adri: A Selfless Scholar of the Maghreb
Biography of Abu Abdullah al-Adri's selfless pursuit of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound selflessness and dedication of Abu Abdullah al-Adri, a scholar who prioritized knowledge and sincerity over worldly gain.

Core Idea
True scholars seek Allah's pleasure, not payment.

This lesson introduces a remarkable scholar from the Maghreb, Abu Abdullah al-Adri, whose life exemplifies the highest ideals of seeking knowledge for Allah's sake. His rejection of worldly compensation for teaching and his humble lifestyle offer powerful lessons in sincerity and devotion.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the personal details and the narrator's firsthand account.
The passage is from Imam Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari.
2
Analyze his fifty-year journey
Consider the sacrifice of leaving family and homeland for half a century. How does this reflect his dedication?
He lived on camel saddles and in inns, showing extreme asceticism.
3
Understand his refusal of payment
Reflect on his reasoning: he feared accepting wages would corrupt his teaching and its reward. He relied only on Allah.
He called teaching his 'most reliable deed' and did not seek reward except from Allah.
4
Examine his humility
Note his refusal of students' help in buying food. He feared it might diminish his reward.
This shows his extreme caution in preserving sincerity.
5
Reflect on his death as a stranger
He died in Qayrawan, away from family, but with the pleasure of Allah. Contemplate the ultimate outcome of his sincerity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدهما أبو عبدالله الأدرى رضى الله عنه وبه انتفع أهل القيروان وترك بها من تلاميذه مبرزین مشاهير جماعة أدركت أكثرهم وكان رجلا ذا علم وأدب أخبرني بعض شيوخنا عنه رحمه الله أنه قال لى خمسون عاما متغربا عن أهلي ووطني ولم أكن فـيـهـا إلا على كور جمل أو بيت فندق، أطلب العلم آخذا له ومأخوذا عنى وقال لى غيره من شيوخنا ما قدر احد من تلاميذه يعطيه على تعليمه له شيئا من عرض الدنيا وكان يقول تعليمى هذا العلم أوثق اعمالی عندى فأخاف ان تدخله داخلة ان أخذت عليه أجرا ولا احتسب اجرى فيه إلا على الله ولقد كان يتركنا في بيته ونحن جماعة ثم يذهب إلى السوق فيشترى غداه أو عشاءه ثم ينصرف به في يده فكنا نقول له ياسيدنا الشيخ نحن شباب جماعة كلنا نرغب فى قضاء حاجتك في المهم العظيم فكيف فى هذا الأمر اليسير، نسألك بالله العظيم إلا ماتركتنا وقضاء حوائجك، فإن هذا من العار العظيم علينا فكان يقول لنا بارك الله فيكم ما يخفى على انكم مسارعون لهذا الأمر ولكن قد علمتم عذرى وأخاف ان يكون هذا من بعض اجرى على تعليمى، وتوفى بالقيروان غريبا رحمة الله عليه ،ورضوانه
One of them is Abu Abdullah al-Adri, may Allah be pleased with him. The people of Qayrawan benefited from him, and he left behind in it from his students prominent, famous ones, a group whom I met most of them. He was a man of knowledge and literature. Some of our teachers informed me about him, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said to me: 'For fifty years I have been away from my family and homeland, and I was only during that time on the saddle of a camel or in a hotel room, seeking knowledge, taking it and having it taken from me.' And another of our teachers said to me: 'No one from his students was able to give him anything of worldly goods for his teaching.' He used to say: 'My teaching of this knowledge is the most reliable of my deeds with me, so I fear that if I take a wage for it, it might become corrupt, and I do not seek my reward for it except from Allah.' And he used to leave us in his house while we were a group, then he would go to the market and buy his lunch or dinner, then return with it in his hand. So we would say to him: 'O our master, the sheikh, we are young men, a group, all of us desire to fulfil your need in great matters, so how about this simple matter? We ask you by Allah the Great except that you leave us to fulfil your needs, for this is a great disgrace upon us.' He would say to us: 'May Allah bless you, it is not hidden from me that you are eager for this matter, but you know my excuse, and I fear that this might be part of the reward for my teaching.' He died in Qayrawan as a stranger, may Allah have mercy on him and His pleasure.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Abu Abdullah al-Adri, one of the two students who came to the Maghreb from the judge's school. It highlights his piety and asceticism. He spent fifty years away from home traveling for knowledge, living humbly on camel saddles or inns. He refused to accept any payment for teaching, considering it his most trustworthy deed and fearing that accepting wages would corrupt it. The passage includes a vivid example of his humility: he would go to the market himself to buy food, refusing his students' offers to serve him, explaining that helping him might reduce his reward. He died as a stranger in Qayrawan.

Key Terms
أبو عبدالله الأدرى
علم
اجر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Scholars should teach for money or status.
Correction: The example of Abu Abdullah al-Adri shows that sincere scholars teach solely for Allah's reward, avoiding any worldly compensation to preserve the purity of their deed.

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Abdullah al-Adri refuse to let his students help him buy food?
A) He was wealthy
B) He feared it would reduce his reward for teaching
C) He did not trust them
D) He wanted to teach them self-reliance

Key Takeaway
Abu Abdullah al-Adri's life is a model of sincere scholarship that rejects worldly reward and trusts solely in Allah's recompense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Would you be willing to spend fifty years away from your family, living humbly, simply to seek knowledge without any worldly recognition? What attachment is holding you back from such sincere devotion?
?
Think of the deeds you most rely on for your salvation. Do you fear that any worldly gain—praise, payment, or comfort—might corrupt them? Will you examine your intentions today and ask Allah to purify them?
?
When you serve others—teaching, helping, or giving—do you secretly expect something in return? Al-Adri feared that even allowing students to buy him food might reduce his reward. What 'small' worldly hopes contaminate your service to Allah?

Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi: The Ascetic Who Saved Kalam in the Maghreb
Biography of Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi, his piety, and his role in preserving knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pivotal role of Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi in preserving the science of kalam and Islamic theology in the Maghreb.

Core Idea
One ascetic scholar saved the science of kalam in the Maghreb.

Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi was not only a pious ascetic but also the key transmitter of the principles of theology (usul) in Qayrawan. In this lesson, you will read a firsthand account of his character, his disciples, and his immense contribution to Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read about his piety and appearance
Read the passage once to understand Abu Tahir's personal qualities: his asceticism, old age, white hair, and tears. Notice how the author describes him as a righteous man secluded at the edge of the city.
Pay attention to the phrase 'غزير الدمعة' (abundant tears) as a sign of his piety.
2
Understand the robe metaphor
Abu Imran al-Fasi said, 'If the science of kalam were a robe, no one would wear it except Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi.' Reflect on what this metaphor tells us about his expertise in theology.
The robe (ṭailasān) was a garment worn by scholars; the metaphor emphasizes unmatched mastery.
3
Recognize his role as a teacher
The passage lists prominent scholars who studied under him, such as Muhammad ibn Sahnun and Ibn al-Haddad. Note the strong claim that without him, knowledge would have been lost in the Maghreb.
This highlights how one scholar can preserve an entire tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانى أبو طاهر البغدادى الناسك الواعظ كان رجلا صالحا شيخا كبيرا منقطعا في طرف البلد أدركته بالقيروان لايدرس لكبره، وكنا نقصده في الجامع لفضله ودعائه وكان يذكر لنا بعض المسائل وشيئا من أخبار القاضى رحمه الله، وكان الفقيه أبو عمران یعنی الفاسي رحمه الله يقول : لو كان علم الكلام طيلسانا ماتطيلس به إلا أبو طاهر البغدادي، وكان رحمه الله اللفظ جميل الشيبة غزير الدمعة كان مليح حسن يظ فى مؤخر الجامع بعد صلاة الجمعة ولم يكن بالقيروان عالم مذكور وهو عالم بعلم الأصول إلا وقد أخذ ذلك عنه كمحمد بن سحنون وابن الحداد ولولاه لضاع العلم بالمغرب
And the second is Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi, the ascetic preacher. He was a righteous man, an old sheikh, secluded at the edge of the city. I met him in Qayrawan; he did not teach due to his old age. We would visit him in the mosque for his virtue and supplication, and he would mention to us some issues and some reports of the judge, may Allah have mercy on him. And the jurist Abu Imran – meaning al-Fasi – may Allah have mercy on him, used to say: 'If the science of kalam were a robe, no one would wear it except Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi.' And he, may Allah have mercy on him, had pleasant speech, beautiful white hair, abundant tears; he was handsome, and he would (?) in the back of the mosque after Friday prayer. There was no renowned scholar in Qayrawan who was a scholar of the science of principles (usul) except that he had taken that from him, such as Muhammad ibn Sahnun and Ibn al-Haddad. And if it were not for him, knowledge would have been lost in the Maghreb.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi, the second student to come to the Maghreb. It describes him as an ascetic preacher, old and secluded. He no longer taught due to age, but people visited him for his virtue and prayers. The great Maliki jurist Abu Imran al-Fasi is quoted saying that if the science of kalam were a robe, only Abu Tahir would wear it, indicating his mastery of dialectical theology (kalam). The passage also notes his physical description: pleasant speech, white hair, abundant tears, and that he used to [preach?] in the mosque after Friday prayers. It then emphasizes his crucial role: every renowned scholar of usul in Qayrawan, like Muhammad ibn Sahnun and Ibn al-Haddad, studied under him, and without him, knowledge would have been lost in the Maghreb.

أبو طاهر البغدادى
علم الكلام
طيلسان
أصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He was the only one who studied it
B) If kalam were a robe, only he would wear it
C) He avoided it
D) He taught it to everyone

Key Takeaway
Abu Tahir al-Baghdadi was the crucial link who ensured the preservation of kalam and usul knowledge in the Maghreb.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were the only person in your city who truly understood and practiced a crucial branch of Islamic knowledge, would you have the ascetic dedication to remain and teach others, even in old age? What would your legacy be?
?

?
Abu Tahir's contribution saved knowledge for an entire region. Think of the people who came after him—countless generations who benefited. Who is depending on you right now to pass on something you have been given, but you are holding back due to comfort or fear? What is your first concrete step this week?
